```
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/2/2040bf49c6a5e924e58de2780c22f7c87654a547.jpeg" width="666" height="500">

Here's my board at the grocery store right now. Brought it up front to check my transmitter is working.  I'm always dropping it 
I'm in San Francisco.  Come over and try these.

Specs? What do you want to know? I don't know the continuous wattage or max. I've hit 45 amps on 12s.  The cheap thin watt meter broke though and I know I can hit any speed of want to go (40?) and almost any hill around.  N45sh curved magnets hair thin airgap and .2mm stator laminations. 100kv. 
I like them a lot with the vesc on <img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/3/3e9e687c5debd3381cbee1e389af9c4ae150b16e.jpeg" width="666" height="500">foc
```

## \#13 Posted by: barajabali Posted at: 2016-01-15T03:13:15.838Z Reads: 1089

```
im not a pro with them, but i have made a pair before that didnt last very long so i can answer lol @NNGG 

They fit on all standard trucks right on the truck shaft like your wheel.
the inner wheel is replaced by the motor stator.
Theyre pretty simple if you have the right tools which are a mill or lathe. 

the problem with mine was that I didnt have a lathe so I couldnt modify the can of the motor for more beefy bearings.
```

## \#22 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-15T03:40:14.098Z Reads: 983

```
These are made by a motor manufacturer in China. One bearing has over double the load bearing of a regular skate bearing and the other bearing is also stronger than a skate bearing.  
The rubber now is 89 duro and I'll be trying an 80 duro next week. 
These mount on a regular skate truck and are glued on.  Glue is strong these days. 
I did a lot of braking in the video. It's almost all ether up hill or down.  There is one very steep downhill almost at the end of the video.  The vesc on foc.  There is more power using the bldc program.  <img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/6/6e3681f9f2717898118c3d044b4448d73e8ea61d.jpeg" width="666" height="500">.
```

```
These are literally R-SPEC quality, except they cost less, and don't require any additional mounting setups! You can kiss risers good by with these bad boys.

I know I'm vouching hard for this guy, but this project is over a year in the making, and he deserves to get 40 buyers for his initial run. And yes, before you ask I am one of them :wink:
```

```
There's a video above of me doing hills in San Francisco. 
I don't know if I'd cal them R-spec quality as I don't know and can't find any ingredients in those motors. I strongly doubt you will find a motor ANYWHERE in the hobby world, that uses .2mm laminations and N45sh curved magnets and a .4mm airgap

If you've done that you're in.
```

## \#35 Posted by: Sharkface Posted at: 2016-01-16T05:00:15.175Z Reads: 801

```
So the gear setup i got from @torqueboards was for 15mm, he just didnt include the proper parts to set it up as a 15mm belt setup. I did just get some parts from alien drive system that are 15mm wide parts. Also I have been talking to enertion about getting some wider setups in stock. 

Make no mistake you will get up those hills with your setup, bumping it up to 12S would make a noticeable difference for keeping speed going up that hill. But a single drive rolling up/down that level of incline is going to get torn up pretty quick. 12t to 36t is going to be the smallest number of active teeth you can roll with that will still work, but it will be rough on stuff. Youll see some good amount of belt slipage. You having a 16t to 36t should be that perfect sweet spot that it will be enough teeth in contact to not slip the belt, but not so many teeth in contact that the belt is getting too much torque put down on it, causing it to snap. (had that happen on the way to the ladies house)

16T motor to 36t wheel on 83mm wheel with a 32v battery powering that 149kv motor will get you that 21mph sweet spot. So your gears are looking dope. You are going to hit the road with that motor and be shocked at how much power you have. when that happens, feel free to message back lololol



EDIT: should include that I didnt ask @torqueboards for 15mm parts, so him sending 9mm parts was expected, just dont know how to throw that in there now that everything is typed out. only mentioning his 15mm so that yall can give him your business for said parts if you so decide lol
```

## \#43 Posted by: cmatson Posted at: 2016-01-17T04:35:34.713Z Reads: 696

```
@NNGG 
 They screw onto the axle where you would normally put standard wheels. 

Depending on your trucks (specifically the length of the axle and it's threads) you might have to do some slight modifications. I believe the cases where modification is needed have to do with the threads on the axle being too short, or just the axle being too short in general- some hanger axles stick out more than others... 

Sorry @Hummie if I'm stealing your replies; just trying to help ya out and get more people on board :wink:
```

## \#50 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-17T07:27:43.309Z Reads: 689

```
the motors will kick out the data center between the wheels on the hanger by 17mm.  Arsenal cast trucks come in 165 and 180 and Paris in 180 and 195 while almost all the other trucks come in 180 and 160. I use the Paris 

I've a set of caliber, Arsenal cast, and the Paris.  The motors fit fine on the Arsenal and I believe the Paris they were fine too, but the Paris had threads that were a bit shorter and needed to be cut with a handheld die. 

For me the biggest question is how to get the trucks to stick on the axle as they're either going to unscrew accelerating or braking depending on which side they are on.   I forget the numbers now but loctite's torque resistance in foot pounds exceeds the torque that these motors can theoretically put out. I did some tests and got roughly 35 foot pounds necessary to turn the same size threading and bolt with red loctite's applied.   (When it does give it doesn't come free really but kinda oozes slowly). The motors might do 16...I forget the formula and need to look it up as someone broke it down based on kv and max power and other things.  Or there's probably a true number of foot pounds these motors are producing I could figure out based on my weight and acceleration speed.  Maybe. So that sounds fine and the glue holds and that's just with red loctite's on the threads but, and I've been discouraged from this worry by others who are engineers, I was worried about the constant vibrations or stresses on the aluminum threading and thought it might break behind the glue.  Aluminum stress cycles leading to cracks. But it's a small space the axle has to move and the threads are deep I'm told and Marc is planning to set up his motors with just the loctite.   I do feel comforted that the glue gives slowly, but I don't like the idea of resting on the threads as he is going to do.  I used j and b weld. But I don't recommend that either as it is too thick to get good surface coverage and avoid any voids, and it is iron filled and not good for vibration and shock and not the best shear strength.  I believe it will be fine but not ideal and a mess to use. There is a better glue that is very thin and double the shear strength used to insert golf club heads into shafts. You know they can't have them flying off. 
I'm torn thinking really the easiest way for everyone whose getting these would be for me to do the glue job as otherwise people will use who knows what, and while that might be interesting to see what holds and doesn't,,,not the safest. 
I'll be having to get more money from people to ship these motors and after seeing what they want to do..hopefully I'll end up buying them all trucks and doing the possible thread cutting and gluing. 
The one downside to the use of such a permenant bond is the big bearing on the inside is trapped. While it's a nice NSK bearing with more than double either dynamic and static load bearing of a typical skate bearing, it might need to be maintained years down the road.  I wont be riding in the rain even when I finally seal up my vescs to protect them as I don't want the bearing in water.  I am thinking when the fat bearing does eventually go dry I can remove the rotors with their rubber, and sink the hanger in a vat of oil and then stick it in my vacuum chamber.  This is the cost for permenantly fixing the motors but it's fine with me.  the other bearing is replaceable and also stronger than a skate bearing in dynamic and static loads.  You guys bought them and I hope you don't feel this is a problem.  If you ever wanted to ship me your hanger I could do it for you free.  Clean it up and spray the windings with more enamel!
```

---

## \#53 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-17T08:13:06.763Z Reads: 568

```
Yes I can cut the threads further so the motors will screw all the way on and I can also permanently glue them if you want. The gluing...I recommend doing it permenantly as I say but three engineers I've talked to about it specifically think red loctite is fine.

Or get a 195 hanger and they are very close in wheel diameter. We're talking 1 or 2 mm. With two 180 Paris it's 14mm difference in wheel spacing.  Not a big deal and really not important at all. Why people don't ride differnet widths ...as long as they fit
```

---
## \#54 Posted by: NNGG Posted at: 2016-01-17T09:16:03.002Z Reads: 567

```
Some thing I did not take into consideration, I have shit roads in my area and my feet and knees get destroyed on a regular longboard with large soft 97mm wheels.And I have to locktight them anyway, so I am worried that the hub motors will suffer from road abuse and the windings or the copper coils in the motor will suffer as a result. I feel a belt setup allows you to switch motors and keeps the motor safe at the expense of belts and gears. The hub motor will have to be disassembled to repaired. Lastly what if the board goes over a curb and other rough terrian, how will the hub motors handle that?

TL;DR I am already invested in a belt setup that I like, know works well and have invested money into. But I like the idea of cheap hub motors $100 versus $80 for a motor and $120 for a mechanical kit even if the hub motors are more vulnerable.
```

---
## \#55 Posted by: lowGuido Posted at: 2016-01-17T10:11:49.480Z Reads: 540

```
[quote="Hummie, post:50, topic:1002"]
The one downside to the use of such a permenant bond is the big bearing on the inside is trapped. While it's a nice NSK bearing with more than double either dynamic and static load bearing of a typical skate bearing, it might need to be maintained years down the road.
[/quote]


I would have to recommend a ceramic bearing for this if you could get one.
I have been very impressed by the way that ceramic bearings handle dust and dirt with absolutely no maintenance whatsoever.
```

---
## \#56 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-17T17:42:50.291Z Reads: 557

```
San Francisco streets can be pretty crappy too.  I've also had one of the motors run over by an suv and its in a video on endless sphere.  

Motor maintenance...there are spaces for screens in the Windows of the motor to keep out debris but I haven't put them in yet.  The windings of a hub motor are probably about as likely to get damaged from rough road vibrations as with an off the side motor mount.   If you're worried about it I've heard of using thermally conductive epoxy. Especially with the low kv motors we use the windings are thinner and have more possibility to vibrate against each other possibly removing enamel and causing a short...although I haven't heard of a case of this specifically happening it makes sense.  The thermal epoxy also helps dissipate heat and you will have a higher power possible. The magnets should be fine as long as the screens are put in these motors. 

The big bearing...either you run use red loctite and later wrench the motor off using a two pin spanner wrench or if it's permanantly fixed on you service it after...awhile. 
I'll look into the ceramic. As it is now and for this coming production it has 2 NSK bearings from Japan and they're really good and much stronger than a skate bearing as I said but if less maintenance is needed with the same ability to take load with ceramic ...and they aren't crazy expensive...maybe go that route next time.
```

---
## \#57 Posted by: NNGG Posted at: 2016-01-18T06:34:24.099Z Reads: 503

```
Are you going to protect your motors from any vibrations and shock, because right now that is a big thing that worries me. A satellite config vibrates the motor from a mount that is not in contact with the ground.
```

---
## \#58 Posted by: elkick Posted at: 2016-01-18T10:47:22.978Z Reads: 517

```
Based on my experience driving hub motors now for 6 month and way beyond 1000km I never experienced that to be a problem. 

And a satellite config is also not really protected against shocks more, it's just the thickness of the urethane. I can't see a big difference.
```

---
## \#59 Posted by: cmatson Posted at: 2016-01-18T15:35:21.835Z Reads: 575

```
@NNGG 

if your motor is mounted to a skate truck it's going to get road vibrations.

That applies to both hub motors and belt configurations. 

On a belt config, it is true that the motor itself doesn't touch the ground, but it's still connected via a solid mount that doesn't absorb many vibrations. It does have a whole wheel to stop vibrations, but that really doesn't make a huge difference compared to the rubber on a hub motor.

I agree that vibrations are slightly more on a hub motor, but it isn't by a significant enough amount to worry about it.  

No matter what, all of our motors are connected to the ground with little to no protection from vibrations anyways.
```

---
## \#60 Posted by: psychotiller Posted at: 2016-01-18T16:28:06.295Z Reads: 615

```
The difference is a hub motor is supporting all of your weight. Vibrations and shock only compound that fact.

Satellite motors are completely isolated from that force. They only have to push our fat Asses.
```

---
## \#61 Posted by: NNGG Posted at: 2016-01-18T19:11:13.074Z Reads: 602

```
That's what I wanted to say, the forces are different on hub motors.
```

## \#62 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-18T19:52:31.260Z Reads: 636

```
But it's doable - holding the two cylindrical planes permenantly within .5mm of each other, even with extreme vibration and shock.   Pediglide is getting good life out of his motors I think, and he did add different bearings and other changes from the original design, which I think is also still going.  My motors have only seen about 130miles so far.  There are other hub motors out there that are surviving. Jason who runs endless-sphere made some long ago and someone on this site and ES made some with cored kegels. I wonder about the big name companies on Kickstarter..have they produced something that lasts or are they pushing back production while they come up with a solution.  E-go seems an extreme example of a board that is constantly breaking and the seller is constantly sending warranty replacements. 

Had a scare lastnight and felt and heard rubbing as I spun the wheels in my hands! Both!  I've redloctited the ring on and wish I'd used something milder as I can't get it off...but blasted inside with air and it's good.  Was thinking for a long time what could've collapsed. 

This is what I want to make!  Imagine the load on those bearings.<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/1/1d6e4064e8b6904611f72dbf37668a8466e078c0.jpeg" width="666" height="500">
```

## \#64 Posted by: psychotiller Posted at: 2016-01-18T20:10:50.823Z Reads: 542

```
@lever is using custom milled endbells that allow for the use of 608 bearings. Those bearings are proven to support weight as well as abuse such as stair gaps and drops.
```

## \#66 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-18T22:05:45.529Z Reads: 536

I'd like to pot the windings in it though but heard that if you have an air bubble it will make things much worse. This doesn't make sense to me

## \#81 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-24T16:53:39.718Z Reads: 484

```
I'll probably do the shrink wrap for you.  Thinking of adding thermally conductive epoxy as well which was mentioned here..to hold the windings better and give them another layer of protection
The bearings I changed to sealed instead of shielded. 
And the magnets are going to be stronger with less high heat potential. This is to add a slightly bigger airgap for safety as people are likely to run their bearings into the ground or not maintain bearing seats with retaining fluid.  Also one side of each bearing will be a shrink (press) fit. Tighter tolerances but still accessible without much effort. 
The problem I had was easily avoided.  Now I could be forced to rewind.  From what I read finding if there are internal shorts in the windings isn't as easy as id hoped.  If I'd measures the windings resistance before running the motor that would've been a help.  I'm thinking it should be in the bldc tool for the vesc!
Regardless rewinding might be easier than figuring out if there are shorts and the temp I got it up to probably damaged the enamel on all the wires.  I'll be riding again within a week no problem 
But there are no warranties as said. But don't worry I expect these to last a lot longer than any other hub motors out there by a long stretch and others all have tiny warranty periods anyway.  If you're bold and use red loctitie to mount the motor (I didn't with these but will be next time), you will be able to remove the motor and replace the big bearing in the back and then these should last you a really long time.  I did testing on the holding power of the redloctite and it will hold the motor's torque no problem....if you want to just use the redloctite there is the danger in my mind of having a wheel fall off from the stresses to the aluminum threading in the motor and it breaking. .  There are shear tests of just such threading and they show to be more than strong enough and a couple engineers say the threading is deep and not to worry.  But that's up to you
```

## \#83 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2016-01-24T21:12:04.895Z Reads: 437

```
I tested these motors and they run great on VESC. I'd recommend them for everyone on flat ground. I wouldn't recommend them for hill climbing especially if over 200lbs+. The motors will heat up too fast and you'll burn them out and it will be done.

You'll still need belt and pulley setups for hills 15%+ and/or for heavier riders.

They are pretty sweet though - hub motors that is..

Just FYI so you guys can manage your expectations... I couldn't replace these with my daily route. I'd burn out these motors quick or have to walk up the hills 15%+. I'm about 180lbs.
```

## \#86 Posted by: torqueboards Posted at: 2016-01-24T21:16:18.079Z Reads: 417

```
You can only at speed and you can't do it often.. Any hill under 15% incline should be fine.. You move higher in inline and these motors will get too hot and burn up.

Flat ground will be awesome with these motors but hills are another story...Not everyone has steep hills though.

Just don't expect these to climb 25% inclines and expect them to keep up with a belt driven setup. It just won't happen.
```

```
At 150 going up 25% you can try... but I highly doubt it.. You'll burn them up quick.. 25% is fairly steep and only belt driven setups would last in this range.
```

## \#90 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-01-24T23:03:27.292Z Reads: 436

```
NNGG it depends how long and steep the hill is and what speed you attack it at and how heavy you are. I'm 160 and did fell street from market st to the park: 

http://www.findhills.com/hill?pagetitle=FindHills.com%20-%20United%20States%3A%20San%20Francisco%20California.%202.70%25%20%28max%2011.45%25%29%201.46%20mi.%26distancein=imperial#location=37.776311856964846,-122.41928100585938~37.77417482537318,-122.43893623352051

That's been the steepest longest thing I've done.  It's about 6 blocks of 9 degree. I've done steeper but not continuously.  As Dexter says these are not the best choice if you want to do long steep things and are heavy.   I did it, it got hot.  I went up at maybe 15mph and down the other side.  Brakes are great. I don't know what temp I hit but if you came here and wanted to try long hills much steeper I wouldn't be thrilled.  It has to be me burning the motors not strangers.  If you really want to do stuff as steep as you say I'd get a pulley board.  Or even pediglide/lever's hub motors are much bigger than these and I bet they could do a lot more.  Or ..get four of these and see what happens. 

There are easier less steep ways for me to get around but I do like to fly up and down hills here late at night.  Too afraid to see what speed I can hit on a flat so I do this.k
```

## \#92 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-02-20T04:17:29.534Z Reads: 473

```
Talked to China yesterday and finalized everything.  Everything I said above but no press fits all tight slide. 
Black rubber 83 duro
Dark purple motors. 
And I'm potting the stators.
With the stronger magnets and slightly bigger gap they'll be more powerful and efficient And the potting should help too.  Now a 200f max temp before can damage the magnets. 

But it should still be 30 business day manufacturing and not including the long two week Chinese holiday.  
Starting whenever I sent it about 3 weeks ago. Maybe 4 forget. Shipping should be quick 
I'm excited for these too because I haven't been riding ever since I shorted. Will be getting vesc back tomorrow and Chaka said they're fine so it's just the motors and have to rewind both.  
But ..no rewinding for you because I'm potting the stators in thermally conductive resin and adding grommets to the wires. 
I'm wondering how people are going to mount them and worried.  I'm going to use actic silver thermal
Epoxy for the shaft and thermal paste for where it butts the hanger.  I think with the two-pin wrench I had made for the backside I should be able to break the epoxy one day and replace the big bearing<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/f/f088ef4914e4958560c62b4c8f752da4bd230628.png" width="281" height="499"><img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/6/6fb36a27888504f98902c5a5ad55c2d16f0bad00.png" width="281" height="499">
Here's a pic they sent me.  U can see there's a very thin purple shim. Another part that I wonder what people will do.  If u look at the exploded 3D u can see where it goes. Figuring the distance between the two bearings and the axial load on them and if it's best in or out is up to you.  I have them in and once the retaining fluid goes on they're pretty stuck.  Next time I'll have them off and have all axial load on the big bearing. Or maybe it won't be all...you can imagine the possibilities.  There's probably a way to decide if it equalizes the load on the bearings or makes things unequal but I didn't take the time and im sure it's fine on or off really. We're taking a .1mm shim I think.
```

## \#118 Posted by: lox897 Posted at: 2016-04-14T09:00:13.845Z Reads: 370

---
## \#119 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-14T15:45:48.680Z Reads: 408

```
Next time I mount some I will make a video.  My iPad doesn't record sound so I'll see.  But visually there isn't much to see and what I'm writing can get you far.  I've done it twice, once with j and b weld, which I don't recommend, just because it's a brittle iron filled resin, and once with two different thermal epoxies.   All of them hold and I'm not worried about them but a resin that is thin and can fill as much of the void between the motor and axle as possible will make a good complete surface the forces the wheel is exposed can buffer, so it's not steel on aluminum threads which could maybe damage the threads eventually.  But maybe it's fine with even red loctite and I've been told that it should be by engineers .  But I don't have a sure solution and am figuring it out myself.  Ideally u could half fill the hole in the motor with something super thin and not brittle and then simply screw the hanger's axle down into it.  But I have t found the best glue and have been having to paint the axle as well as a bit inside the motor hole and screw tightly.   I marred up my screw notch on the motor badly when the blue stuff was super thick and I couldn't screw the motor all the way down. That is important.  U don't want any exposed axle and the motor and hanger should touch. My second shot I warmed up some thermal epoxy, the white stuff from Omega, think it was number 100, and it was much thinner and better but not as good as could be found.  I'd forget trying to get something thermally conductive and just try to find something thin.  Do a bit of research or ask someone what would be thin (less viscocity), and not brittle when cured, and a bit of modulous of elasticity(I don't know)...and tell me if u find something good

!!! Also I ran out of shrink wrap and refuse to buy it at the rediculous prices at the hardware store so some of u have none extra, just what they came with and it s far from enough.  Check that there is enough there.  I added two later to what was there for most of the motors.  And I didn't put the screens in to protect from debris, get some at the head shop probably.  !!!
```

## \#126 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-17T22:23:36.616Z Reads: 393

```
The good news is I don't even try to race boosted guys.  It's no race on any terrain. And I can woop on spandex clad cyclists at a moments notice with even the 80kv.  Peak speed about 26mph. The instant peak power is more so than the last motors it feels and I can accelerate from 5 to 25 quicker. The bad news is this motor gets hotter than the last.   I just raced my friend to the beach and back on his bike through the partially closed golden gate park and crushed him and could stop and chat along the way...but was at 220f at the end .  Probably the longest sustained power output I've ever done.  The bad news is the blue potting I did was stupid and detrimental.   Get an infrared thermometer and monitor.  Sorry guys.  So peak power still rocks but long sustained runs the heat doesn't disipate well
The magnets are rated to 212f and they shouldn't see as high heat as the stator.
```

## \#128 Posted by: laurnts Posted at: 2016-04-18T00:02:36.431Z Reads: 365

```
To reduce heat (dissipate heat faster).
```

---
## \#129 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-18T00:08:39.129Z Reads: 370

```
The first reason wa to fix the stator which was becoming loose on its aluminum seat.  I think the increase of thermal expansion of aluminum compared to the steel stator had deformed the aluminum under the stator. maybe. Anyway I thought the blue goo could hold the stator and also transfer heat to the aluminum wall beside it and the skate hanger beyond.  I went overboard and covered half the breath holes as well as covering the winding on the other side as well. Dumb.
```

## \#148 Posted by: monkey32 Posted at: 2016-04-24T20:56:22.213Z Reads: 370

```
@Jack The outside flange (purple) that holds the urathane on the motor is held in place by 6 screws..........between each screw holding the flange - (see last photo with purple flange) is a ~7mm hole. The motors need some more ventilation and a screen to keep sediment out of the motor itself. The flange is ~ 6cm diameter......with "vent holes" centered   ~7.5mm from the edge of flange. What would be considered the exterior of the motor or the face the flange presses up agaianst - the outside face of the hub.....has a recess ~1cm in diameter which would take the screen or could be used as a foot.


The first two pictures are the motor hub with urathane mounted without the purple flange (you can see the recessed area)

The final pic is the motor with one screw holding the flange on the hub.
```

---

## \#154 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-25T18:12:15.300Z Reads: 342

```
The blue goo is everywhere. A mistake. The benefits are that it'll keep the windings secure.  The bad news is it makes the motor hotter.  I'm riding with the blue goo and the motor's peak wattage is still great but the continuous wattage is decreased with the heat build up.  Ride it.  See how it does.  Talk to me if u have a problem.  If it's an issue we can work it out.  I'm in the blue goo now and it's good.   U won't be able to remove it

U still need to glue the motor on the skate axle. Other than that there is nothing else to do
```

---
## \#155 Posted by: barajabali Posted at: 2016-04-25T18:24:04.815Z Reads: 330

```
Oh okay I have to epoxy it on. Do I just put epoxy on the axle and screw the motor on? Easy enough.
```

---
## \#156 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-25T18:28:40.646Z Reads: 333

```
I haven't discovered the best way to do it but at this point I've found thicker epoxy is hard to screw into and heating the epoxy will make it thinner.  
So far I've used j and b weld, good but brittle and not the best, and two high heat epoxies.  Use two-part, high heat and longer cure time stuff and warm the parts first. 

Unless u use a really thin glue, if u can find one, paint the axle and the hole and screw it in. Try to get as much in there but not overflow and get it on the bearing!
```

---

## \#158 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-25T18:37:35.314Z Reads: 352

```
The purple plates hold the rubber on.  Screw them to the black motor with the screws. Don't drop a screw in the wrong hole.

Lever is on the war path and I'm here to cover my bases!   These motors go and go well.  Disappointingly I put thermal epoxy on all of urs.  Idiot.  The motors are solid though and I ride all the time and have no issues with anything related to the motor.  The softer rubber I'm finding will overly soften and deform from the high heat and I'm thinking the 89 duro, which I've done over 200 miles on and hit 220f with, is good though.  More than good. 

I'm not looking to follow a path of problems with this design and other than needing harder rubber I'm also going to be getting the compete motor made in steel
So the bearings can be pressed in. Solid. As it is now its an aluminum shaft using retaining fluid to do a close eproximation of a press fit.  
But fear not, U will not break these motors as is though and at worst u could have a bit of rattling and want to open it up to add more retaining fluid. 
Anyone who got these from me I won't leave u dangling..if u have a problem with ur rubber we can work it out
```

## \#167 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-26T04:01:46.502Z Reads: 381

```
I was just thinking about machanical issues and I've been thinki and saying the only hurdle is mechanical.  

I'm so impatient I got 120 motors after only having ridden the prototype maybe 200 miles before it shorted.  It's all very experimental and I discovered problems and won't go into them but now... I'm ready to move away from these motors because they have an aluminum center.  My first motors were silent for the short time they were going.  My new 2 motors have also done maybe 150 miles and one is rattling.  I could press it open with a simple press but the ring is loctited with red and even my special tool for the ring won't budge it without a lathe chuck or something to clamp it.  Open it.  Clean the bearing seats with a knife, squirt more on,  get it back together, and hope for the best and listen.
The manufacturer will do the same motors with a steel center instead of the purple aluminum.  Heavy but solves the stator spin problem and the stator can just be pressed on, but more important the bearings can be pressed on.   

I'd like to see how ur putting urs together Jerry. What are the bearings sitting on and press or slide fit?  


I hate rattling. I more so added retaining fluid (on the motors I sent) on the aluminum side. The aluminum side can't move or the aluminum might deform.  

It's hard to sell something, I have 70 of, when I'm already excited about the steel one.   but we will see


If anyone wants to do it in steel the manufacturer said it would be the same price! I thought that was great. Anyone who wants in on that...whatever the minimum order quantity I can get it down to.   I'll be going back to work at saving my dollars.  I'll sell anyone an aluminum center one 100$  I get them for 64.50 and then PayPal and shipping from China and another  3 from PayPal when people buy them and me pouring the rubber. 100$. Anyone who wants an aluminum or steel!  The aluminum I'll send u immediately and the steel...once we can get enough orders

I ride the aluminum now.  Or did till today as my receiver keeps conking out after bashing it.  Very scary and it locked me on throttle and I had to abandon ship.  Running running and over falling. But not a scratch.

Or maybe I just need some higher heat retaining fluid.
```

## \#173 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-26T17:22:40.200Z Reads: 377

```
Nice.  Ride those wheels and I'll send u some black in the next month no cost except shipping

Guys these motors don't break at 200 miles!  These blue ones in particular get hot and maybe that's what it is but the retaining fluid has vanished on one of my motors and it rattles.  It rattles less than a regular wheel but to solve the rattle the motors need to be opened and maintained.  It's a pain. Maybe mine is the only one that will rattle. Maybe no one else cares if theirs rattles a bit.  
It is very rare to find a loaded bearing on an aluminum shaft and that's what these motors are.  It's a big anodized aluminum shaft but none the less it's aluminum.  These seems typical as I know Jacobs motors are aluminum with a smaller shaft and a slide fit.  (It has to be slide fit because u need to take it apart to replace the rubber.  These motors are intended to be non-openable so that the tolerances can be kept minimal. U have to press these motors apart not simply undo some screws and it falls apart.  Especially on an aluminum bearing seat it needs to be fixed or things will wear. But u getting an interference or press fitting on aluminum especially with its much larger than steel thermal expansion..not ideal.   If the motors were all steel, not half steel, they could be pressed steel as mechanical parts should be.   But   I was told aluminum would do, and it does, but requires retaining fluid.  This is simply glue for bearing seats and makes an effective press fitting. As long as it stays put the motors are silent.  Maybe it was temperature related and I over cooked it.  Maybe there's another higher heat stuff.  There probably is a better one and I just jumped on whatever was handy. Loctite makes a million things.

Hitting 220f likely is the cause as well as hitting 180
Often.   I'm sorry the blue goo was a mistake.

Just telling u how it could go.  At worst you'll have a rattle that will take some elbow grease to get rid of. 

I designed these motors for me foremost and I'm picky.   Their performance is fantastic. The only problem is a potential rattling.  I hope people who got these have an infrared thermometer and keep track of their temps and if they do and up with a rattle that annoys them I can send u in the right direction and lend u the tools to open it up and fix it
```

## \#181 Posted by: laurnts Posted at: 2016-04-26T21:35:13.860Z Reads: 324

```
Hi @Hummie returning from the questions you asked earlier about the mounting of the chinese hub motor, I think I understand your question.

Ive just did another hub motor inspection and I found that I could just remove the Hub motor cover (those tiny 6 little m3 bolt) without first opening the m8 hex bolt that keeps everything in place. Therefore the bearing has no retaining fluid on the inner side and both bearings inside the hub motor handles no side load torsion.
```

## \#182 Posted by: exco Posted at: 2016-04-26T21:47:30.393Z Reads: 347

```
My first post - so hi to you all on eSk8.

[quote="Hummie, post:129, topic:1002, full:true"]
The first reason wa to fix the stator which was becoming loose on its aluminum seat.  I think the increase of thermal expansion of aluminum compared to the steel stator had deformed the aluminum under the stator. maybe. Anyway I thought the blue goo could hold the stator and also transfer heat to the aluminum wall beside it and the skate hanger beyond.  I went overboard and covered half the breath holes as well as covering the winding on the other side as well. Dumb.
[/quote]

Maybe the [Arctic-Alumina-Thermal-Adhesive](http://www.amazon.com/Arctic-Alumina-Thermal-Adhesive-5g/dp/B0009IQ1BU) (2k thermal compound) could be interesting for what you are trying to do.
It's quite expensive @8$/5g though.

Regarding really strong 2k glue I would recommend [UHU Endfest 300](http://www.amazon.com/epoxy-resin-adhesive-Double-syringe/dp/B000WGYSVO) 
Whenever I need glueing that lasts - that's what I use and it has never failed.

It is rated: tension and shear resistance (aluminium) [datasheet](http://www.nikhef.nl/pub/departments/mt/projects/KM3NeT/Referencedesigns/DOM_DigitalOpticalModules/Ref5/Drawings/uhu_plus_endfest_300_eng.pdf)
10 hours: 500N/cm²
24 hours: 1200N/cm²
5 days: 1700N/cm²


Also if you heat it with a hot air gun to around 50°C it will be thin as water - just be careful not to make it too hot or it will deteriorate.
```

## \#186 Posted by: exco Posted at: 2016-04-27T00:09:33.594Z Reads: 347

```
Actually - if you think about it some more - this isn't a bad idea.

At least if you modify it a bit:
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/1/181aed3167b8da4204653bb658caf4ceca9f58e3.png" width="690" height="253">

This is just a really fast mockup for visualization.
The green screw represents the truck axle,

If you bore out the motor e.g. to 8.05mm (this is vastly exaggerated in the picture)
and have e.g. 8mm tapped on the outside to screw on the motor.

This way it will be locked by the nut.

I haven't calculated it though - if it can hold the acceleration/braking torque,
but if it does there is no need for glue anymore.
```

## \#195 Posted by: baxter Posted at: 2016-04-27T13:08:05.484Z Reads: 362

```
I am fairly new to e-boarding, so I hope you will forgive my naivety about the methods for securing hub motors to trucks, but I have been wondering why I haven't seen anyone use a circular clamp method in the style that's used for conventional satellite motors to trucks.  Using the truck clamp from @torqueboards v4 mount as an example, if this clamp or something similar were strategically bolted (or welded) to the inner end of the hub motors, (around where the axle would be) it could make life a lot easier for securing the hub motor to, or even changing your trucks. 

Yes there might be some aesthetic issues to work through, but it would be much simpler than worrying about the chemical and physical properties of epoxies to keep your motor(s) secure :slight_smile: .

@jacobbloy
@LEVer  

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/a/a2ff9a0591c4979dcfb32cff0b25d4d401348ec3.png" width="291" height="299">
```

## \#198 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-27T16:33:20.091Z Reads: 349

```
But glue is strong.  Glue can be much stronger than the power of the motor.  They say glue holds planes together these days. 
  I've done tests and even red loctite on just the threads need 35ft/lbs to turn and when it does turn it barely turns and the motors might put out 10ft/lbs.  But I don't recommend  loctite as more so the worry to me is the forces going through the aluminum sitting on the steel axle.   A buffer between the two is good.

It's common for typical outrunner  to have their stator glued to the bearing tube.  They have keyways cut in the stator but I've never seen them used and it's just a press fitting with some glue.  The torque applied to the motor on the skate axle is the same force on this stator to bearing tube connection and I don't hear of them spinning....unless they're on solid aluminum where the aluminum expands and deforms.
```

## \#210 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-27T22:04:05.618Z Reads: 335

```
skate axles all have the same threading but just different lengths along the axle.    

Mine have 4 layers of shrinkwrap and it becomes kind of rigid and sticks out and there's nothing Needed to hold it.  I've got Velcro holding them comin out of the vescs.   Turning is not a problem as the wires all come to the center of the truck [Uploading...]() 
I did get lucky with a symmetrical wire set up, actually I think it's probably because the epoxy I used was too thick and the motor didn't bottom out.  

Check ur motors and feel how solid they are. Any movement in bearings or the axle especially is no good.   Talking of tight fittings, and keeping the competition fierce, lever's motors up till now at least, are a mismatch of an 8mm bearing 
sitting on a 5/16 inch axle.  True that's what they do in the skate world and I can crank them down so there's no play, and I do, but in an electric motor u won't find that happening. I don't know if retaining fluid could even fill a gap that size.  We should expect it silent and solid.

And the rubber. Check it competely for movement before u get it going.  feel it when its hot.  Be aware
```

## \#219 Posted by: jacobbloy Posted at: 2016-04-29T17:03:54.938Z Reads: 339

```
Hey mate really!
I have made an effort not to even post here but
http://www.electric-skateboard.builders/t/the-nicest-hub-motors-for-sale-cheaper-than-anywhere/1002/205?u=jacobbloy

"The most efficient hub motors out there"
Blatant lie or your just and idiot!

Customers are complaining your motors are getting to hot a 0.2mm stator lamination isn't going to help that there getting hot because your winding has a high resistance. Every motor factory (tiger motor, scorpion, hacker, maytech including my factory have 0.2mm lamination you didn't invent this)
Making your motor rated up to 200deg won't make any difference. Ferrari don't have a powerful engine because it's rated up to 1000deg it's because they engineered good breathing and cooling and made the dam thing efficient.

I remember a conversation with Theo from inboard that I had while helping them with there design, I suggested to use 45SH magnets because of the heat rating he said "jacob why would I ever need this? I would never let my motors go over 60deg"

This is true and some thing you should really work on.

Low efficiency produces heat, high resistance produces heat, to much eddy current leakage can produce low efficiency and finally to much eddy current can produce heat.

You talk about bearings bearings bearings and tolerance and glue but do you even know how to fix any of these efficiency's because these are the most important parts to a hub motor because if you don't fix them then go back to a belt drive and don't waist the time and money!

Choose your reply carefully because if you reply with a smart ass comment or some thing bad about my motors in return then ppl might actually see that you don't know what you are doing when it comes to the actual electrical engineering aspects of these motors.
Or you could head to google or wiki or some of the very educated members of this forum who might help you and fix the dam problem!
```

## \#220 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-04-29T18:32:48.300Z Reads: 348

```
You don't know what ur talking about yet calling me an idiot. 

The reason some of the motors are getting hot is because they have thermal epoxy in some of them and it retains heat. 
My windings have the lowest resistace possible because it's single strand copper. The only thing that will beat that is silver single strand or graphene if it ever comes out.  Look it up. Learn it.  Then try to make urs that low resistance and while ur at it how but telling us what urs is!!

I didn't invent .2mm laminations and as u say there are some manufacturers that use it.  How much do they sell their motors for?  Huge cost. What's YOURS?   You will not find anyone running .2mm stator lam motors on their board unless they spent at least 250$ for the motor alone. Most of the motor manufacturers u listed will SOMETIMES do a .2mm stator but often it's .25.  Look it up.  These are where the majority of the iron losses come from especially because with a hub motor's fewer commutation sleep hysteresis lower. Look it up and learn and the get back to me when u know what you're talking about

Temperature?  U don't know what ur talking about and I'm not impressed with your name dropping.  If you research scorpion motors or other motors that have higher performance it's often because they use higher heat magnets enabling the motor to go to higher heat and therfore higher wattage.  Look it up.  Do a search for scorpion high heat magnets. In fact they use weak magnets so they can get higher temp ability and they make up for it wth a smaller airgap
 
"Low efficiency produces heat, high resistance produces heat, to much eddy current leakage can produce low efficiency and finally too much eddy current can produce heat.".
  I don't think u know what ur talking about again and if anything your explaining why my motors are more efficient than ANY motor you will find.  Sure low efficiency and high resistance produce heat.  My motors are more efficient then yours because I have single strand wire, and they limit eddy current way more then yours because of the thin stator lamination.  What strand count and how thick are your lams?  Air cooling.. I have room for air turbines in my holes and I'll be sure to show u the results when they come in 

Smart ass comment?   How bout u respond to my questions above and we can get some other people around who know something and we can show you how electronic motors work 

My motor will crush yours or any other in terms of efficiency because of the reasons I've listed.  Find someone to tell me otherwise and I'll give you a kiss.   I also have a super thick shaped flux ring/rotor while yours...see what happens when you put iron on the outside of the rotor.  Theres your wasted flux.  

I had a batch of stupid thermal epoxy experimentation and hope to get unadulterated motors in their hands.  I'm willing to lose money on this.   Anyone who bought a set of the blue motors I'll send a set of the better motors for 100$!!!plus shipping.
```

## \#227 Posted by: jacobbloy Posted at: 2016-04-29T23:24:00.380Z Reads: 342

```
How about you tell us your winding turns and you say it's single strand!

Well these are the 2 winding photos I have found
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/f/f87ea23756b3b5d708e1ad42eb396fa047d5391e.png" width="281" height="499"><img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/0/074be8a97a2a9f83f0f1bafd3ed37b482b20ea5f.png" width="281" height="499">

Know maybe I am an idiot and it hard to know from a photo but it doesn't look like you are using a Wye winding (if you are my mistake I just can't see) but in a delta winding to get 80kv in your size stator you would be using a 20-25 turn winding, this means there is no way you are using a thick copper and in the pick you can see that so let's say you are using a 1.0mm copper strand which as about right for the picture, for a winding you need to take 3 things into account (turns,resistance and the copper cross section)
The copper cross section is what sets your amp limit.
So the copper cross section,  say you used 1.0mm copper in a single strand your cross section will be 17.28
Your resistance 163.7mOhms
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/5/5901441e49a2a0ce51fac6c47db35466d02f5ee9.png" width="489" height="500">

My motor is 24 slot so apples to oranges:
Cross section less at 10.97
But my resistance is less at 130.8
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/4/4c7965520c3d3fe70c615c7a2d2c6fc72f902c43.png" width="489" height="500">

And while we are at it here is my 0.2mm laminated 24slot stator <img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/7/7bf7eb8df2d4f5930550d60ad0ee98d2e29369ee.jpeg" width="500" height="500">
```

## \#251 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-05-05T19:38:07.454Z Reads: 328

```
I've been riding the unadulterated (non-blue) motors the last two days.  The good news and the bad news.:
My testing of the different motors ( 100kv, N45sh magnets, .4mm airgap; 80kv, blue thermal motors, N50m mangnets, .5mm airgap; 90kv, N50m, .5mm airgap) isn't so scientific and the unscientific results are continuing for the next hour!:slight_smile:

So far it's showing that all end up with similar heat except the 90kv seem to rocket up hills faster than any of them ( u all have 80kv).  My test of seeing the temp a tthe top of my local hill isn't so good because I can get up there so fast with these motors.

Racing myself to the beach and back and see what temp I hit now

The bearings I'm disappointed becaus rim getting s bit of seizing even at only 150f and it could be that little spacer!  Or not. 
I'm learning myself here and want to go steel and pressed bearings with .4mm airgap and the high temp magnets.  That would be the machine that will have no problems.  I also have a little rattle with these new unblue ones I'm riding.  Disapointing.  As long as ur aluminum side is secure though it's steel on steel and ok as I say. 
That's the somewhat bad news, the other bad news is I'm retracting the offer of 100$ for a pair of these aluminum ones if u already bought a set of the blue. They're too similar and u won't notice much if any temp difference.   I can't be losing money on these and I am left and right.  But but...anyone who buys a set at the 300$ cost or already got a set I'll sell u a set of the all steel pressed bearings with the .4mm airgap and N45sh magnets( they hit 300f) at the manufacturers cost which they're now saying is 65.50$ That machine will be Solid.  Bit heavier but there's more important things 

Seems someone has taken my design and run with it.  I shouldn't have maybe said so much as the manufacturer is had other people asking for my motors and they're saying they will alter the design and sell them!!  Wow and theyre barely tested. 
The goal is a solid ...sollllid..motor which can hit high temp no problem and won't suffer from thermal expansion or retaining fluid issues.  Steel is the answer to a lot more power and solving all mechanical issues. 

I hope u guys are into this and we can head this direction down the road.    The aluminum rock and mine are going strong ..bit of rattle and a max temp of 200f I don't like though.
```

```
I have to say, I can't tell if its the difference between the carvons and hummies motors, or the difference between 12s and 10s, but they had way more power then I expect. Starting from stop like a champ. My carvons can start from stop, but not with the power these things had. Running hummies motors at 12s is felt really solid. Again, I did 3 back and forths, so I can't speak about hills or reliability yet. But my initial impression was that these motors have a lot of torque, way more than my carvons (and that makes since, 90kv compared to 145kv, you'd expect the lower kv to have more torque). The question will also be in the top speed. I ride my carvons at 25-30 mph as much as possible. Idk if 30 mph is possible with these, or for extended periods of time.

I will be doing more side by side comparisons with hummies 80kv motors and the carvons soon. I need the rest of the truck parts from hummie tomorrow, and waiting to get my carvons back becuase guess what, machining into the hanger to attach the motors creates a weak spot, and mine bent. So I'm waiting to get the back. Either way, I will be testing both vigorously and comparing the 2 as best as possible, using the same setup but with different hub motors.

I am a hard rider. I punch the throttle to its limit, I like speed. As someone who has ridden a skateboard almost every day for the last 10 years (minus the 3 surgeries I had due to skateboarding), I push the boundaries of what should be done on a skateboard.. I pushed the carvons, and they broke. They will  (be fixed, and we will see if they break again. I will push hummie's, and see if they break. If so, I will take them to hummie, have him do what he can, and push them till they break again. The hope is not to break them, the hope is I never have an issue. The problem is, everyone wants to say they have the best shit. Well, send said shit my way, and I will tell you if it can hold up to my 195 pounds, steep hills, and very aggressive riding. So far, Enertion - Failed (could work, but what I was (told to buy and) sold was not what I needed. I needed a larger belt, this wasn't an option at the time. When told I was breaking belts left and right,I was told it was my fault. The problem was, 9mm single belt on steep hills means belts break every 3 weeks. But instead of point me to a larger belt elsewhere, he says its my fault), Carvon - Failed, but redemption is possible (Jerry has been extremely nice to me, and willing to repair them with my only cost being shipping in one direction), and now Hummie's - Unknown... It will be interesting...
```

## \#268 Posted by: onloop Posted at: 2016-05-08T08:20:03.420Z Reads: 371

```
[quote="evoheyax, post:267, topic:1002"]
So far, Enertion - Failed (could work, but what I was (told to buy and) sold was not what I needed. I needed a larger belt, this wasn't an option at the time. When told I was breaking belts left and right,I was told it was my fault. The problem was, 9mm single belt on steep hills means belts break every 3 weeks. But instead of point me to a larger belt elsewhere, he says its my fault)
[/quote]

most people should know by now that there are people who do actually use 9mm wide belts on a single drive successfully... I certainly don't recommend it though... so it's unlikely i forced you to buy them against your will, you put them in your cart & paid for them didn't you?

other contributing factors to broken belts are:
1. poorly aligned motor mount
2. wobbly wheel pulley
3. over tightened belt.
4. ESCS with no/limited throttle & brake force control functions 

I made this video which clearly explains what you should have.... using a VESC is recommended as you can control brake force.

https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eakga9Bzj9E
```

## \#275 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-08T09:42:57.117Z Reads: 331

```
Because I was a newb at the time, it was my first build. And I wanted to keep as low budget as possible. The impression given was that dual drive was unnecessary. Why sell a product period that could easily brake? If I ever have the chance to sell a board, I wouldn't do less then dual, because I don't want a customer to be bummed out. I'm impressed what a single drive could do, so a dual? The reality is, I had other issues too. Debris from the messy, construction crazy San Francisco get into the belts. Lots of pebles, dirt, and sand (according to jerry from carvon at least).

To pull it back on topic however, My whole point of joining this discussion was to make one point, which is having gone from a signle drive belt, to a dual hub, and now another dual hub, I feel like hub motors like hummies are a glimpse of the future of e skateboards. FOC and 100% in-wheel motor. Compaq, yet full power. I'm ready to take them on.

My only thought is, bigger wheels? I like the carvons abec 11 90mm wheels. Super smooth riding.
```

## \#288 Posted by: HTownBomber Posted at: 2016-05-09T16:27:59.352Z Reads: 301

```
I'm skeptical that the rattle is caused by bearing compression. Bearings are engineered to handle high compression forces. That tiny bit of thermal expansion from  aluminum probably won't deform the steel inner ring of the bearing, and certainly won't damage the steel balls inside.   

Bearings aren't engineered to resist high temperatures or lateral forces. I'm thinking that the heat is breaking down the lubricant. Maybe put some speed cream or high - temp oil/grease in the bearings. That or they are misaligned from the lack of a shims, and lateral stresses are damaging the raceways. 

Just a guess. Let us know how they look when you open them up.
```

---
## \#289 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-05-09T16:38:42.246Z Reads: 305

```
Opening didn't happen.  I tried and the red loctite didn't give using my huge 2-pin spanner and a table clamp. 
Strangely I was riding with evoheyax yesterday and his ring unscrewed itself.   I'll have to make a mold of the rotor outer grooves out of a soft metal that can be used in combo with the table clamp so I can really wrench on it
Ur motors are in the mail days ago htownbomber 

The rattle issue isn't the bearings themselves but the surfaces they sit against. A bearing is intended to be pressed into two steel surfaces: the shaft and housing, but I'm using high heat retaining fluid which is really an epoxy glue intended to make an effective press fitting while using tight slide fittings. The lateral forces and heat on the bearings is well within their specd ability.  If the bearing to steel bell/rotor interface becomes a looser fit it will rattle and that's been the issue.  I haven't had any bearings lose the tight interference fitting in the aluminum shaft side and that is the real concern.  A slide fitting on an aluminum shaft bearing heavy loads isn't good.  
Anyone who got a set from me is eligible for an all steel set and pressed bearings and back to the .4mm airgap and N45sh 300 degree temp magnets when they come in soon at the same 100$ each price That's the shit and I make pretty much no money considering the cost to me for the motors and my making of the wheels.  You will not damage those steel going up a mountain or riding down the gravel path on the backside.  The aluminum are still going strong anyway and the worst I've experienced is a slight rattle similar to a typical 5/16 inch skate bearing on its 8mm axle 


http://www.nsk.com/products/spacea/high-temperature/
```

---

## \#309 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-05-10T17:14:30.355Z Reads: 267

```
Yea there no point in testing now since the steel is going to happen.  A relief. 
In the future I'll mount the motors because I know it's a pain for each person to go through it and it adds to the cost while if I do them all its cheap. 

I like omega thermal epoxy number 100 in the little envelope they sell.  10$ and ud need two. But any high heat, two part, preferably slow cure epoxy will work.  Try to find high heat stuff and that's a bit harder and you'll likely have to get it online.  Heat it in the oven at 150f to make it thinner, mix it, pour into the motor hole half way, screw in the axle.  Clean the axle with acetone first. Don't get it on the bearing!  Use tape to make sure 

U really only need a bit of
Loctite on your ring and you'll be fine.  It will rattle a bit probably but only steel on steel. Sound like a regular skate wheel
Or open the motor and add "retaining fluid" to the two exposed sides of the bearings that sit in the bearing housing/rotor. The bearings already have it on the inside against the shaft and will be stuck there.
```

## \#321 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-05-10T17:57:19.818Z Reads: 254

```
Both of ur motors have the big black threaded ring on the back of the motor loose.  The little purple shims save somewhere. Loctite both of the big threaded black rings that hold the motor together.  It should be pretty easy to tighten the ring but maybe have something that u can use to get into the ring's holes and help tighten it.  When it's tight, and the bearings are in the right place, you'll have no lateral movement in the motor.
```

## \#337 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-05-15T04:54:36.023Z Reads: 293

```
Thanks for the nice words. 

<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/1/17b0a324bfabf2aa2f01abbe053f7b5e233db54b.jpeg" width="666" height="500">
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/8/8d2b5baf92c214c41291a7536feaa127b1858c8a.png" width="375" height="500">


the best part about buying these is if later you decide slide fitted bearings and aluminum shafts are for weight weenies and you want to get the all steel pressed bearings motor...you can have them for the same price. 

These are two rare sized 57mm motors not 63mm.  If you feel you're more than my 155lbs and will be doing long steep things Jacobs are a safer bet in that regard.  But I have no problem blasting around San Francisco of sustained 8 blocks of steep climbing.  

These match the kegel wheel size/shape and are recessed in the wheel.  Good for sidewalk cracks and not feeling you're on a hot rod.  

These are sealed motors with effectively press fitting on all bearing contacts. You can have a sealed motor, solid, if you are able to replace the rubber without having to open it. 

There is less leverage on the axle with these and the motors on 165 hangers match the 180.  They don't stick out and add leverage to the axle

Im getting adapters made now, to add air forced air cooling through the holes that hold the screens.  If u feel a need for more cooling things can be done. Lately I've wanted to take some kryogenic fluid like a co2 canister and blast them half way going up my tam here.  My goals are to be able to ride mountains on these and you're in if you're in

Finally, and I've said it before, mechanical challenges are what is most important for You to think about.  How long is an electric skateboard hub motors supposed to last??? Warranty??? I'm offering solid steel with minimal large parts and the largest bearings.  Ask a machine shop which they'd chose and go with their advice.
```

## \#352 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-05-16T20:27:20.919Z Reads: 287

```
thats a putty and too thick.  

the omega 100 sets much quicker than what you wrote and i think youre describing their 201 stuff.      they have different ones.  from now on ill do it for people but still that doesnt help you now.  

get two of the omega 100 small envelops maybe.  but remember it has a quick set time.  its good, thin, high temp stuff though.  put it in the oven at 150f for 10 minutes then mix the two, pour half way in the motor hole and then screw in the axle.   dont get it on the bearings and use tape to make sure.
```

## \#359 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-17T05:00:50.798Z Reads: 299

```
torque is by far better, top speed is much less. But I can't notice much of a difference in top speed, as the highest I've gotten my carvons is 35 mph, and the highest I usually would cruise at any distance at is around 30 mph, and these max out around 27 on a 12s, so you won't notice much of a difference in top speed. Mostly, you'll notice these motors pick up really well.

With this version, the only problem you'll notice could possibly be heat. And that is only after long distances up hills. For medium to short rides, or flat ground ridding, there's nothing better out there IMO. Even if you get too much heat, you can stop for a few minutes, the heat will go down and you can keep riding. I did a test run with hummie using these riding for around 40 minutes on flat and some hills, and never had an issue with heat. Only time heat was a problem was when I rode uphill for almost 3 miles straight.

Overall, they are solid, and with the option to buy the steel ones (which should eliminate all possible problems with these) for only 225 later, they are a great deal. I'm glad to have a pair of carvons, but I think these will become my main motors when I build a better deck this summer.
```

## \#382 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-20T21:44:12.138Z Reads: 278

```
Like I said before, I can't imagine the carvon single having the power you want. 2 motors will always be better than 1. It's more money as you need another esc, but there's a huge increase in performance. These guys have more torque than the carvons, due to the lower kv, but the carvons single might get 3 or 4 mph faster. TBH, at those speeds, 1 motor when breaking is scary. Using one motor makes the board want to turn real quick on brake/acceleration. If you don't make the correct weight shifting adjustments, it will throw you off, which has happened to me before. I thought it was bad at 18 mph, I can't imagine single drive braking at higher speeds.
```

---
## \#383 Posted by: elkick Posted at: 2016-05-21T12:19:54.851Z Reads: 299

```
Some others builds. No issues at all yet, and I don't expect any after the first tests.
```

## \#388 Posted by: evoheyax Posted at: 2016-05-22T17:21:29.580Z Reads: 272

```
It could just be my set up, but that's what I've experienced. Its not to say, you don't get used to it for the most part. I didn't notice it most of the time, but subconsciously, I was putting a bit more pressure in one direction. There are times when I was thrown off the board when breaking at speed because it jerked a bit ad I didn't shift my weight accordingly. I guess I should say you can overcome the pull. It also be partly be caused by not using a vesc on that setup too. If I hit the throttle too quickly, it definitely pulled harder the truck one way. I feel more comfortable on a dual drive setup though, as there is no pull one way or another.
```

## \#417 Posted by: cmatson Posted at: 2016-06-03T02:05:06.106Z Reads: 302

```
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/2/226b12c83af6a112bd36e4a80026a3a1ce5d364f.jpg" width="519" height="500"><img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/4/445886b48a30694ba801fc530b413ad8e5087591.jpg" width="523" height="500">
<img src="/uploads/db1493/original/2X/c/c7c06e7f4b22c2495d556278b0284f73615c5c89.jpg" width="560" height="500">
so I had to get it to fit in this bag, which requred me to move the rear trucks all the way back on this little board.. Also, on the second hub (since both were glued at the same time) I made sure the motor wires are each insulated from each other before wrapping them around the truck with duct tape.

**I was so thankful I had a @RunPlayBack enclosure though, because without it I'd be toast and boardless in Australia for 5 weeks!!**

anyways, @Hummie I only weigh about 135ish, so the single hub should be able to handle me fine for the 5 weeks I'm down in Australia; after that, it'll be back to the plan of dual and 10s4p. I don't plan on pushing the board hard either, as it will mostly just be used in conjunction with uber and public transportation. This is more so just a mellow sightseeing board that I can cruise around town on. 

I also ran it for about 3-4 miles today, going somewhat fast. Not pushing the acceleration hard, but cruising around 18 I'd say. When I got back, I was able to hold the motor on both sides without getting burned or feeling like I'm getting burned, so I'd say it isn't all that bad. Plus, that distance at that speed won't happen very much while I'm on my trip, because like I said I'm just going to be using it for transportation and sightseeing.. not blowing by bikes in the bike line or climbing any hills. 

Final point.. Someone buy these hubz! everybody be freaking out over this steel issue, but they are torquey as all get out (on a single hub too!) and definitely beat my old enertion 5065 245kv in all around performance. An RSPEC 6355 is still more powerful as a single, but I think these in a dual config would be able to beat that single RSPEC, and probably even the single 6372.
```

## \#442 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-06-06T16:49:29.644Z Reads: 262

```
From FAA:

Spare (uninstalled) lithium ion and lithium metal batteries must be carried in carry-on baggage only. When a carry-on bag is checked at the gate or at planeside, all spare lithium batteries must be removed from the bag and kept with the passenger in the aircraft cabin. The battery terminals must be protected from short circuit.
This covers spare lithium metal and spare rechargeable lithium ion batteries for personal electronics such as cameras, cell phones, laptop computers, tablets, watches, calculators, etc. This also includes external battery chargers (portable rechargers) containing a lithium ion battery. For lithium batteries that are installed in a device (laptop, cell phone, camera, etc.), see the entry for "portable electronic devices, containing batteries" in this chart.
Size limits: Lithium metal (non-rechargeable) batteries are limited to 2 grams of lithium per battery. Lithium ion (rechargeable) batteries are limited to a rating of 100 watt hours (Wh) per battery. These limits allow for nearly all types of lithium batteries used by the average person in their electronic devices. With airline approval, passengers may also carry up to two spare larger lithium ion batteries (101-160 watt hours). This size covers the larger after-market extended-life laptop computer batteries and some larger batteries used in professional audio/visual equipment.
Quantity limits: None for most batteries – but batteries must be for use by the passenger. Batteries carried for further sale or distribution (vendor samples, etc.) are prohibited. There is a limit of two spare batteries per person for the larger lithium ion batteries described above (101-160 watt hours per battery).
Batteries must be protected from damage.
Battery terminals (usually the ends) must be protected from short circuit (i.e., the terminals must not come in contact with other metal). Methods include: leaving the batteries in their retail packaging, covering battery terminals with tape, using a battery case, using a battery sleeve in a camera bag, or putting them snugly in a plastic bag or protective pouch.
See the regulation: 49 CFR 175.10(a)(18)
Tip: Newer lithium ion batteries have the watt hour (Wh) rating marked on them. To calculate watt hours, multiply the battery voltage by the Amp hours (Ah). To learn more about lithium batteries, their restrictions, and how to tell what size they are, go to http://SafeTravel.dot.gov
View our illustrated guide on Airline Passengers and Batteries (PDF)."



Seems u could have an unlimited amount if they're small
```

---
## \#443 Posted by: Jinra Posted at: 2016-06-06T16:55:27.009Z Reads: 247

```
I've read up a bit on this since I'm flying out to Japan in September. I plan to rig up 2x 160wh batteries for transport and all laws seem to line up with my plan. As for larger 18650 packs, Jason has brought his space cells from Hawaii back to Aus with no problem. A lot of people don't really know what they are or don't care. Not recommended to do, as it's very likely you can get your packs confiscated. @appelton should probably reconsider. I doubt getting caught lying about the wh on your battery will go very well.
```

## \#454 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-06-09T18:55:29.050Z Reads: 253

```
the vesc's battery and motor current limits are important and really effect the performance!!

In the past I've shown I can go up hills much faster on the 80kv vs 100kv motors but this need not be the case!  I've had my motor current limit at 60 always and with the higher kv motors they need more amps to make the same torque, so if the motor amp limit is increased they will get the same uphill performance.  They will still produce the same heat as with the lower kv and the less amps (thicker windings on the higher kv and less resistance).   the only reason not to up the possible amps to the motor would be if ur concerned about over cooking the motor. If ur concerned u could always drop the number way lower and never think about it...I prefer to get as much power as possible and just be aware of my temp with continuous output and consciously slow down of my own volition instead of being limited to something lower than the peak possible power output

volts are converted to amps by the vesc so running higher voltage will keep the vesc temp down (it does have a safety shut off thankfully), but the motor only sees it as amps...so using 12s will allow u to push the vesc to a higher output but the motor doesn't experience a difference between 6 or 12s assuming it's gearing or kv is appropriate 

If u got motors from me and don't know how to mount them get a small envelope of the omega 100 thermal epoxy and extract half, heat to 150, mix, pour in the hole and screw in the axle, repeat. All the other epoxies are too thick to do this with and not as good
```

---

## \#457 Posted by: PB1 Posted at: 2016-06-21T14:09:49.482Z Reads: 232

```
I mounted my Hummies last weekend and can share some of my learning: 
Set time of the Omega 100 is pretty short, according to the spec sheet between 6 and 12 minutes. Which is not a lot. It's also somewhat thick. If you heat it up e.g. put the package into hot water, it gets thinner and easier to work with. However, heating it decreases set time even further. 

So my recommendation: 
- do one wheel at a time (prep, mix epoxy, pour, screw in axle), then do the other
- get a good, **really big** screw driver
- don't pour in too much epoxy, if you do, you will not be able to properly screw in the axle 
- you can shim your motors by using speed rings so that the wires come out boardside of the trucks. 
- if you want to make a video, use a tripod or another person as you will be pretty busy already
- turn down the sensitivity of the microphone. The likelihood that you will be using bad language while mounting the motors is pretty high
```

---

## \#465 Posted by: PB1 Posted at: 2016-06-22T06:07:51.942Z Reads: 247

```
@surprisebirthday, how much epoxy? If your axle is properly threaded and goes in all the way you don't need much. Just imagine,  your axle will go in all the way,  then where is the epoxy supposed to go? It will either spill out or your axle is stuck, depending on the cure time of the stuff.  You only need epoxy between the axle and the wall of the hole.  
For my second axle I actually put the epoxy on the axle,  then screwed it in.
```

## \#475 Posted by: Mobutusan Posted at: 2016-06-22T20:23:47.480Z Reads: 238

```
@elkick Thanks for the confirmation/feedback. Glad to hear I won't be the first Loctite guinea pig. 

@Hummie I wouldn't think there should be any more alum/steel contact with the Loctite compared to epoxy. ## \#532 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-06-26T21:46:52.297Z Reads: 242
```

```
u can remove the purple anodization form the aluminum parts i read with drano. i forget which drano exactly and im not sure if regular works. if u do a search youll find it. u want to let the parts sit in it and then remove them when the color is gone, but not too long as there will still be a coating of anodization thats clear and will protect the aluminum. dont get it in the windings and maybe only do the bolt-on flange
```

## \#549 Posted by: elkick Posted at: 2016-06-28T06:43:53.430Z Reads: 219

```
Maybe you can give these values a try:

_Motor tab:_
Motor Max 40
Motor min (regen) -30
Batt max 20
Batt min (regen) -20
Absolute max 100

_BLDC tab:_ 
min ERPM: 50
min ERPM int. Limit: 600

_Advanced Tab:_ 
Startup boost: 0.030
```

## \#555 Posted by: Maxid Posted at: 2016-06-28T08:01:33.406Z Reads: 203

```
How come you recommend not using FOC on your website but are using it yourself?
I am still undecided if I should try FOC - scared it might fry the DRV.
```

---
## \#556 Posted by: elkick Posted at: 2016-06-28T08:12:38.890Z Reads: 206

```
Because when I destroy a VESC with FOC I am not calling the manufacturer to replace it on warranty. It's my own risk. 

But having seen that so many people blow their DRV chip (whatever the reasons might be), providing warranty on this would mean to finance other peoples hobby with my money and I can't afford that. FOC is still in experimental phase.
```

---
## \#557 Posted by: Maxid Posted at: 2016-06-28T08:14:59.933Z Reads: 206

```
[quote="elkick, post:556, topic:1002, full:true"]
FOC is still in experimental phase.
[/quote]

So is it being worked on? What needs to be done? To me it looks like all focus is on VESC6 and not FOC for older revisions. Do you have any idea what is actually causing the damages in FOC mode?
```

---
## \#558 Posted by: elkick Posted at: 2016-06-28T08:15:10.414Z Reads: 194

```
@Hummie, first it's battery charge capacity which might be limited, but also to get the heat down for for both, acceleration and braking.  The above settings (only motor tab) are working for me also uphill. It might depend on your specific setup though.
```

---
## \#559 Posted by: elkick Posted at: 2016-06-28T08:24:06.657Z Reads: 201

```
Only theories: some motors are working, some others don't. Also, not resetting the FW to factory values before switching between BLDC/FOC can cause that damage as well. 12s seems to be more often causing  VESC failures in general than lower voltages, since you are close to the limit the VESC can take. Not much margin there.

Benjamin is working on the firmware for BLDC and FOC for both versions V4 and V6, so not much difference. But it might be, that the new DRV for V6 is generally more robust.
```

---

## \#609 Posted by: 3sly Posted at: 2016-07-03T20:31:51.961Z Reads: 190

```
Yep I get what you wanne say (I'm currently an aircraft/aerodynamics engineering student :p). I solely meant that the oncoming wind might be to strong vs the forward centrifugal force. But the longer I think of it that probably won't be an issue as the main goal is to draw air from inside the motor, and that will happen in any case (and I think that's probably what you wanted to explain). Testing will show the extent of the effectiveness. But as I've said before: great job and very nice idea.
```

---
## \#610 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-07-03T20:46:07.443Z Reads: 196

```
I'm getting simple radial blades made as well as 1/4 turn blades which are similar to what's shown above but instead of 45 degree angles it will be a compete 90 degree. With the 90 degree blades facing backwards the on-coming air pressure will always be attempting to get in the hole at the bottom of the wheel as it spins.  Any spinning wheel is stationary at its lowest point just as it touches the ground.  It is not moving forward into the wind at that point in its revolution and will have the least forward air pressure at that point.
```

---

## \#612 Posted by: Ulfberht Posted at: 2016-07-04T00:35:05.402Z Reads: 186

```

Maybe a screen and filter on the intake side of things?
```

## \#613 Posted by: Mobutusan Posted at: 2016-07-04T01:25:06.572Z Reads: 180

```
I still like my ducted ram air concept. Force clean, screened air toward the inside of the hubs, and push heated exhaust air out the outside of the hubs.
```

## \#614 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-07-04T01:43:58.476Z Reads: 191

```
the motor has spaces for small screens on the outside face between the motor and bolt-on flange.  there arent places for screens on the other side but i do want to get them there.  a simple scoop like you did mobutusan would go well with the part im getting made.  im getting one with plain radial blades and another set with a twisted pinwheel blade that finishes 90 degrees from where it started.  all of them will blow air out regardless of the direction its spun.  see which one does best and which direction.
and the big scoop one is done ...i'll tell you how they do in a couple days.
```

---
## \#615 Posted by: Hummie Posted at: 2016-07-04T02:19:46.181Z Reads: 210

```
[quote="devin, post:611, topic:1002, full:true"]
[quote="Hummie, post:610, topic:1002"]
Any spinning wheel is stationary at its lowest point just as it touches the ground.  It is not moving forward into the wind at that point in its revolution and will have the least forward air pressure at that point.
[/quote]

ii think the outflow becomes pushed to a standstill at the very front of the wheel by the 20mph oncoming air but emerges from the top, bottom and behind the wheel.
[/quote]
 the oncoming air, 20 mph, would reduce the amount of air that could exit.  its pushing the other direction.  it would be a counter force against the direction wanted. we will see. i think the 90 degree spun blades sweeping backward will only have openings for the oncoming air at the lowest point in the rotation, and then have no frontal air to force through and so more going out..cooler motors
```
